FOR DECENCY
WINS A POINT
"Little Egypt" Heav
ily Fined.
POKER MEN APPEAR IN COURT
CARE EXERCISED IN DRAWING
UP THE COMPLAINTS.
Judges Conlan, Mogan and Graham
Will Each Have a Chance to
Determine What Is the
Law.
The cases of the poker-player? arrested
Monday night were distributed in Judges
Conlan, Mogan and Graham's courts
yesterday, the eight men arrested In the
Metropole being in Judge Conlan's court,
the six in the Cafe Royal in Judge Slo
gan's court, and the eight in the Palace
In Judge Graham's court.
When the cases were called In each
court the came procedure was gone
through. Attorney Ach appeared for the
defendants and by consent the cases were,
continued till Saturday to enable the ar
resting officers to simi complaints after
they had been drawn up by the prosecut
ing attorneys in each court. Saturday
the defendants will be asked to plead
and n dutc will be fixed for the trial of
the cases.
Yesterday afternoon Prosecuting Attor
ney Joachimsen of Judge Mogan s court
had the six complaints for the Cafe Royal
cases drawn up and they were sworn to
by Sergeant Conboy before the Judge.
The complaints recite that the defendants
"did willfully and unlawfully open and
conduct and carry on a certain percentage
game and there and then played with
cards and then and there played for
checks, and then and there being repre
sentatives of value in lawful money <>f
the United States to wit: that a certain
percentage game known as poker in a cer
tain public place situated to wit: at and In
a house and place known as No. 801 Mar
ket street in said city and county."
H. A. Horlein, the proprietor, is
charged with "permitting a certain per
centage game;" Joseph Barry with "con
ducting a certain percentage game" and
F. H. Ryder, Peter Hayes, Thomas Sono
gini and' A. Austin with "playing a cer
tain percentage game."
The defendants in the Metropole cases
in Judge Conlan's court are L. H. Han
pen, proprietor; John Wilson, conductor,
anr] Frank Winn. W. Pnrker. C. Sipe, Al
fred Berand, Julius Klein and Bud Wil
liams, ]>la\ers. In the Palace casos in
Judge Graham's court the defendants are
C. W. Rebeman. proprietor; J. 11. Wil
son, conductor, and Fred Meyer, Herman
Hoffman, Victor Josselyn, John Diener,
Alfred Brandenberger and Thomas Han
sen, players.
When "IJttlfi Egypt," convicted by
Judge Conlan Monday of committing a
lewd and indecent act In . her contortion
dance at a theater on Market street, ap
peared for sentence yesterday Attorney
Long moved for a new trial and arrest of
judgment. The Judge, after listening tr,
hit* arguments, refused the motlf.n and
sentenced her to pay a fine of $100 with
the usual alternative.
Attorney Long gave notice of appeal
and the bonds were fixed in $300, which
were at once forthcoming. The case for
trial by jury in acting Police Judge Par
ry's court will not coma up till May ifl.
A Hoodlum's Punishment.
George Cameron, alias. Collins, a typical
hoodlum, was convicted by Judge Slogan
yesterday on charges of disturbing the

MINISTERS WILL OPEN FIRE TO

Oakland Office Snn Francisco Call,
908 Broadway, April 26.
The Alameda County ministers have
prepared a statement to be submitted at
the regular prayer meetings on Wednes
day evening, expressing their regret that
Oakland should take up with and en
dburage an evil that even t^un Francisco
has dispensed with.
The protest is as follows:
We, the pastors and churches of
Alameda County desire to enter our
respectful but emphatic protest
against the receni action "f those di
rectors of the Fabiola Hospital who
voted to accept the proceeds of the
so-called Derby day at the Emery
ville racetrack, and against their an
nounced determination to make this a
"gala day" and a "society occasion,"
thus countenancing this gigantic Â«-vil
and encouraging and aiding an insti
tution which is damaging to the busi
ness and moral interests of our com
munity.
We further desire to express our
appreciation of me noble stand taken
by those other directors of Fabiola
who made the earnest, endeavor to
prevent this Derby day, but who were
defeated by a vote of 20 to 13
This recent action of the Kahiola di
rectors in their affiliation with a
gambling institution is more deplora
ble in the light of the recent action of
the city government of San Francisco
in banishing pool rooms, and the vig
orous efforts of our Oakland city offi
cials against all forms of gambling.
We should teach our people to glad
ly share their substance for the relief
of the unfortunate rather than that
our charities art- to be supported by
connivance with gambling institutions

Dismissed by Stipulation.
The suit of the Mutual Electric Light
Company against Mayor Phelan and the
Board of Supervisors, wherein the com
pany sought to compel the board to grant
it permission to erect poles outside the
fire limits, was dismissed yesterday by
stipulation. The dismissal "of the suit is
the result of the board's action in grant
ing the covetfd privilege.

SOCIETY OF CALIFORNIA
VOLUNTEERS AT BANQUET
VETERANS OF THE CIVIL WAR
ELECT OFFICERS.
Will Request First Regiment of This
State, Now in Manila,, to Perpet
uate Their Organization.
The California volunteers now in Manila
will on their return homo he asked to join
the Society of California Volunteers,
which is composed of veterans of the
Mexican and Civil wars. This action,
taken at the thirty-fourth annual meeting
of the society held last evening at the
Occidental, is intended to perpetuate the
organization. President C. W. Gordon,
who presided at the meeting, stated that
the invitation to the younger soldiers
would undoubtedly he accepted, and he
appointed a committee, consisting of
Charles A. Sumner, Colonel W. R. Smed
berg- and Colonel C. Mason Kinne. to con
fer with the regiment when it comes back
and persuade them to fraternize with the
older volunteers.
The election of officers to serve for the
ensuing term resulted in the selection of
Captain Charles A. Sumner as president;
J. 11. Gilmore, first vice president; 11. J.
Brady, second vice president; James I>.
Homer, corresponding secretary; C. W.
Gordon, treasurer; J. C. ]nnes, recording
secretary.
After the business meeting the members
adjourned to the dining-room, where an
elaborate banquet was enjoyed. Retiring
President C. W. Gordon acted as toast
master, and in his introductory address
Btated that the society had gathered to
properly celebrate the anniversary of the
day on which General EL V. Sumner as
sumed command of the military forces on
this coast thirty-eight years ago in place
of Albert Sidney Johnston, and thereby
prevented the loss of California aa a
member of the American Union.
The following were the toasts and those
who responded: "President of the United
States," Captain Sumner; "Our Country,"
Captain H. A. Gorley; "Army and Navy,"
( olnnel W. R. Smedberg; "Our Society,"
c W Gordon; "California." C. Mason'
Kinne; "The I'nion Dead," Captain Elisha
Brooks.
Besides the honored guest of the
evening Rev. John A. B. Wilson, pastor
of Howard-street M. E. Church, there
were also present William McCleave, J.
H Gilmore, J. Ellis Hill, Captain John
Lafferty, H. J. Brady, Colonel J. B.
Moore G. A. Bwasey, G. B. Tolman,
Major William B. Hooper and J. C. Innes.

RECITAL BY
ROSENTHAL
After an absence of several months,
Morltz Rosenthal returned to San Fran
cisco and played yesterday afternoon in
the Grand Opera-house. His programme
was an excellent one and his playing was
quite as sensationally obstacle-proof as
it was at the previous performance, but
the audience was notably small, in spite \
of the low prices. A good-sized audience j
Is half the success of a concert, and It i
seems a pity so few of our musical towns- !
folk should have turned out to greet an j
artist of Rosenthal's importance.
His playing needs no new description. !
From a technical standpoint . he is the
wonder of the age, and he has a fine mu
sicianly mind that asserts itself in every- !
thing that he approaches. That !â <â â  has
not the ideal temperament, the human
throb, is perhaps to be regretted," but it j
is not a newsy regret at this time of day.
We must accept Rosenthal's tempera
mental limitations in much the same j
spirit that we accept those of Henry j
Irving. Both are great technical artists,
and have done something for the develop
ment of their. crafts. ;.-;:;
Rosenthal's most distinguished work
yesterday was in Beethoven's "Appas- I
sionata" sonata, which he played with j
rich, sonorous tone and authoritative an- !
alysis. . The rest of the programme dis- j
played the artist in a variety of moods \
and aroused the genuine enthusiasm of 'â 
those present.
In the same theater he will play this !
afternoon the following programme:
